Pending  - Dependency: Requires accurate COGS data from "Completed" stage to calculate Net Profit; - Dependency: "Stalled" logic requires defining time thresholds per stage.                                                                             \nFolder highlights\nBlueprint details the 10-stage Antigravity workflow from Lead to Completed, emphasizing data-driven transparency and defining the "Zero Surprises" Promise.\n\n# 1. LEAD (INTAKE & TRIAGE)\n\n> [!IMPORTANT]\n> **One True Source (OTS)**: This document governs the logic, UI mapping, and operational mandates for Stage 1. It bridges the public website, internal intake tools, and the triage AI.\n\n## 1. Stage Mission & Core Metrics\n- **Mission**: Convert "Curious Visitors" and "Action Seekers" into structured Property Leads.\n- **Success Criteria**: Every lead must have a verified address, a Timeline (Shopping vs Ready), and a Path Assignment (A-E).\n- **Key KPIs**: Lead Capture Rate, Triage Accuracy, Time to Response.\n\n## 2. App Page Inventory (Blueprint Mapping)\n*Mapping from Master Page Registry (APP PAGES.xlsx.csv)*\n\n| Page ID | Name | Route / Component | Primary Function | Priority |\n| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |\n| **P-01** | About Us | `/about` | Tech-Noir Identity & Trust Building | High |\n| **P-02** | Our Services | `/services` | Capability Catalog (Residential vs Commercial) | High |\n| **P-03** | Our Process | `/process` | 10-Stage Visualization (Anxiety Reduction) | Critical |\n| **P-04** | Financing | `/financing` | RPSP Logic & Payment Terms Disclosure | High |\n| **P-05** | Contact | `/contact` | Directory & Direct Founder Access | High |\n| **P-08** | Public Estimate Tool | `/estimate` | Instant Ballpark (Path A/B Generation) | High |\n| **E-02** | Global Lookup | `(Internal)` | Universal Property/Customer Entry Point | High |\n| **E-02a** | Customer Input | `/customer-input` | Dynamic Intake, Routing & Photo Capture | High |\n| **E-26** | Lead Stage Page | `/admin/leads` | Employee Holding Pen / Triage Management | High |\n\n## 3. Logic Engines & Gates\n\n### Universal Triage Engine (Paths A-E)\n*Governed by [IntakeTriage.tsx](file:///c:/Users/mjrob/OneDrive/Desktop/App%20Repo s/RHIVE-OS-1.0/components/IntakeTriage.tsx)*\n\n| Path | Profile | Action Gate | Resulting State |\n| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |\n| **Path A (Ballpark)** | Curious / Shopping | Timeline: "Shopping" | Ungated Estimate (P-08) |\n| **Path B (Action)** | "Ready to Roll" | Timeline: "Ready" | Certified Quote + Sched (E-02a) |\n| **Path C (Inspector)** | Damage / Emergency | Toggle: "Leak" or "Insurance" | Forced Inspection Workflow |\n| **Path D (Specialist)** | Manual / High Touch | Selection: "Call me ASAP" | Priority CRM Callback |\n| **Path E (Referrer)** | Abundance Network | Param: `?ref=...` | Referral Tracker Activation |\n\n### Commercial/Government Mandate\n- **Input**: If Property Use = "Commercial" or "Government".\n- **Rule**: Bypass "Ballpark" automation.\n- **Output**: Lock pricing; direct user to "Schedule On-Site Inspection" (E-02a).\n\n## 4. UI/UX "Tech-Noir" Directives\n- **Visual Hooks**: Neon-pink progress indicators, high-contrast imagery, and the **Transparency Grid** on the estimate results.\n-Terminologies: The phrase **"Lifetime Installer No-Leak Guarantee"** must be visible on P-01, P-02, and P-08.\n\n## 5. Operational Commands (Human/AI)\n1. **AI Assistant (E-03)**: Must interpret rough intake notes and map them to the proper triage path.\n2. **SOP**: "Never reveal pricing to a Commercial lead without an inspection signature." \n3. **Escalation**: Triage failures or "IDK" paths are routed to **Lead Stage Page (E-26)** for manual oversight by Maureen (Admin).\n\n## 6. Integration & External Sync\n- **APIs**: Google Maps (Address Verification), Google Static Maps (Visual Intake).\n- **Webhooks**: Zoho CRM (Lead Creation), Twilio (SMS Callback Alerts).\n\n---\n**Version**: 2.6 (Indexed Enterprise)  \n**Status**: ACTIVE  \n**Last Sync**: 2026-02-09
1      Stage 2: ESTIMATE (Item Catalog / Ballpark)                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                        \nFolder highlights\nBlueprint details the 10-stage Antigravity workflow from Lead to Completed, emphasizing data-driven transparency and defining the "Zero Surprises" Promise.\n\n# 2. ESTIMATE (PRECISION MATH & TRANSPARENCY)\n\n> [!IMPORTANT]\n> **Master Stage Document (MSD)**: This is the "One True Source" for Stage 2.\n> **Vision**: The "Tech-Noir Juggernaut" — delivering ineffable quality via AI automation to render competitors obsolete.\n> **QCI Rating**: 1,000,000 (Targeting Signal Density & Brand Resonance).\n\n## 1. Stage Mission & Core Metrics\n- **Mission**: Provide an automated, high-precision ballpark range that builds trust through radical transparency.\n- **Success Criteria**: Estimate is calculated within 2% margin of final quote (based on user inputs).\n- **Key KPIs**: Estimate-to-Quote Conversion, Math Accuracy Score, RPSP Promo Redemptions.\n\n## 2. Integrated App Page Inventory\n*Linked from Master Page Registry (APP PAGES.xlsx.csv)*\n\n| Page ID | Name | Route / Component | Primary Function | Priority |\n| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |\n| **P-08** | Public Estimate Tool | `/estimate` | Anonymous Ballpark Pricing & Lead Capture. | Critical |\n| **A-03** | Estimate Pricing | `/admin/pricing` | Global Math Controls: Waste Logic, Rate Tables, Pitch Factors. | Critical |\n| **A-04** | Estimate API | `/admin/api` | API Endpoints for external tools & Website Embed Codes. | High |\n| **E-02a** | Customer Input Page | `/sales/input` | Dynamic Intake, Polyline Measure Tools (Gutters/Heat Trace). | High |\n| **E-16** | Income Actionator| `/sales/income` | Real-time commission simulator based on Estimate logic. | Critical |\n| **E-18** | Report Builder | `/sales/reports` | Slide Forge: Converts photos/math into PDF Proposals. | High |\n| **A-05** | Line Item Catalog| `/admin/catalog` | Master Material/Labor logic with Photo/Video library. | High |\n| **C-Tracker**| Customer Tracker | `/portal/tracker` | "Pizza Tracker" transparency for the homeowner. | High |\n\n## 3. Logic Engines: The Roofing Math Engine\n\n### Geometric Analysis (Vector Math)\nThe system analyzes 3D property data (Google Solar API) by evaluating vertices $(x, y, z)$.\n- **Eave**: External Edge + Horizontal ($|z1 - z2| < 0.1$). Calculates Gutter/Drip edge.\n- **Rake**: External Edge + Sloped ($|z1 - z2| \geq 0.1$).\n- **Ridge**: Shared Edge + Horizontal + Convex.\n- **Hip**: Shared Edge + Sloped + Convex.\n- **Valley**: Shared Edge + Concave (Determined via Dot Product vs. Centroid).\n\n### Precision Pricing Pipeline\nThe final retail price follows the **Transparency Model**:\n\n$$TotalRetail = \frac{(Material + Labor + Overhead)}{(1 - 0.25)}$$\n\n- **Material**: Dynamically pulled from **A-05 Line Item Catalog**.\n- **Labor**: Calculated by Square count $\times$ Pitch Tier Rate.\n- **Waste Factor**: \n    - **Global 10%** standard.\n    - **Facet Logic**: < 5 Facets = 5%; 5-15 = 10%; 36+ = 22.5%.\n- **Pitch Tiers**: Standard (3/12-6/12), Steep (7/12-9/12), Critical (10/12+).\n\n## 4. Psychometric Calibration (The Omni-Bird Engine)\nDifferent customer personas require tailored data presentation to maximize trust.\n\n| Persona | Focus | Directive |\n| :--- | :--- | :--- |\n| **🦅 Eagle** | Bottom Line | **BLUF**: Show total price, current lead time, and "Lock Price" CTA immediately. |\n| **🦉 Owl** | Data/Logic | **Tech-Grid**: Expandable view of facet counts, pitch tiers, and material spec sheets. |\n| **🕊️ Dove** | Safety/Harmony | **Guarantee**: Highlight "Lifetime No-Leak Guarantee" and the "Integrity Fee" (Profit). |\n| **🦜 Parrot** | Energy/Novelty | **Visuals**: Trigger the Slot Machine Ticker and 3D color-coded model on load. |\n\n## 5. Sales Framework Integration (Oren Klaff / Dan Martell)\n\n### Oren Klaff: Frame Control & Intrigue\n- **The Why (60%)**: Public Estimate Tool (P-08) lead with *why* transparency is the new standard.\n- **The Intrigue Gap**: Ballpark is revealed, but **Precision Data** (the etc. gap) is withheld behind the "Certified Quote" gate (Frame: Authority).\n- **The Scarcity**: "Prices validated for 14 days only due to material volatility."\n\n### Dan Martell: Revenue Acceleration & Systems\n- **Revenue Maximization**: Automated "Upsell Triggers" (E-18). If Roof Age > 15yrs $\to$ Trigger "Solar Prep" or "Gutter Replacement" logic.\n- **Scalable Operations**: Logic supports Level 2 PM capacity (managing 640 projects/year) through zero-manual-math automation.\n\n## 6. Logic Engines: The Construction Command\n\n### The "Live Construction Feed" (E-32 -> C-03)\n- **Mechanism**: Integrated mobile camera access for Crew Leads.\n- **Categorization**: Photos are tagged by stage: `TEAR_OFF`, `DRY_IN`, `FLASHING`, `COMPLETION`.\n- **Sync**: Uploads instantly appear as a "Story Mode" style slider for the customer in C-03.\n- **Trust Factor**: AI auto-captions the photos (e.g., "Your old shingles have been removed! Readiness 100%").\n\n### Change Order Triage (The "Frictionless AWO")\n- **Field Step**: Crew identifies rotten decking or extra flashing. They snap a photo via E-32 and enter the dimensions (e.g., "3 Sheets of Plywood").\n- **Office Step**: PM receives a push notification -> PM verifies the unit price (Admin can override) -> PM clicks "Send for Approval."\n- **Client Step**: Customer receives an SMS link to a **Mini-Sign Page**.\n- **The "No-Stop" Rule**: Work continues while the link is in the air. If the customer hasn't approved within 15 mins, the AI Bot (Twilio) triggers a "Courtesy Call" to explain the necessity of the fix.\n\n### The "40% Draw" Automated Trigger\n- **Condition**: Once the PM clicks the **"Verify Substantial Completion"** button (Roof is watertight/done).\n- **Logic**: \n  - 1. Sum original contract balance (Draw 2).\n  - 2. Sum all *Approved* AWOs.\n  - 3. Generate Invoice.\n- **Action**: Invoice is pushed to the Customer Portal and emailed instantly. The status moves toward Stage 8 (Punch List) if items like Gutters remain.\n\n## 4. The "Trade Handoff" Wizard\n- **Logic**: Upon completion of the primary trade (Roofing), the Crew Lead fills out the **Trade Handoff Form**.\n- **Selections**: \n  - `READY_FOR_GUTTER`: Notifies the Gutter Crew + Schedules MS-4 Logistics.\n  - `PUNCH_LIST_NEEDED`: Routes to Stage 8 (E-33) with specific defect tags.\n\n---\n**Version**: 1.1 (Indexed Draft)  \n**Status**: ACTIVE  \n**Last Sync**: 2026-02-09

Columns: [SYSTEM ROLE: RHIVE "Omni-Bird" Psychometric Analyst
Identity: You are the world's most advanced behavioral psychologist and roofing sales strategist. You specialize in the "Omni-Bird" framework, which fuses DISC, Transformational Leadership, and Enneagram motivations into a visual avatar system.
Objective: Analyze raw customer communications (texts, emails, notes) to construct a "Psychometric Digital Twin" (The Omni-Bird). You must output a strict JSON object that drives a 3D visualizer and provides specific sales scripts.
1. THE "OMNI-BIRD" DECODING LOGIC
Step 1: Determine Base Species (DISC Style)
Analyze tone, speed, and focus.
EAGLE 🦅 (Dominant): Direct, brief, results-oriented. Keywords: "Cost," "Timeline," "Now," "Contract."
PARROT 🦜 (Influential): Enthusiastic, social, scattered. Keywords: "Beautiful," "Excited," "Neighbors," "Design."
DOVE 🕊️ (Steady): Patient, loyal, hesitant. Keywords: "Safe," "Warranty," "Family," "Trust," "Guarantee."
OWL 🦉 (Conscientious): Analytical, precise, skeptical. Keywords: "Specs," "Data," "Research," "Process," "Numbers."
Step 2: Assign Hardware (Innovation & Pace)
Headgear (Openness/Innovation):
Circuit Crown 👑: Asks for "modern," "newest tech," "solar," "Tesla." (High Originality).
Stone Helmet ⛑️: Asks for "proven," "standard," "traditional," "reliable." (Low Originality).
Propulsion (Pace/Urgency):
Jetpack 🚀: Short sentences, urgent requests, "ASAP." (Fast Pace).
Anchor/Backpack 🎒: Long paragraphs, detailed questions, "No rush." (Slow Pace).
Step 3: Assign Armor (Emotional Stability)
Chrome Plate 🛡️: Stoic, logical, formal. No emojis, strictly business. (High Stability).
No Armor (Feathers): Emotional, reactive, uses emojis, expresses worry/excitement. (Low Stability).
Step 4: Assign Wing Tips (Core Motivation)
Gold Tips ✨ (Status/Success): Wants the best-looking roof, wants to impress neighbors.
Blue Tips 🔵 (Accuracy/Knowledge): Wants to be right. Cites research.
Green Tips 🌿 (Harmony/Peace): Wants to avoid conflict and feel safe.
2. ROOFING CONTEXT RULES
The "Leak" Variable: If the word "leak" or "damage" appears, heavily weight Urgency (Jetpack) and Stability (Feathers) unless they remain unusually calm.
The "Price" Variable:
Eagle asks price to negotiate/decide.
Owl asks price to analyze value.
Dove asks price to ensure safety/affordability.
Tie-Breaker: If D and I scores are equal:
Prioritize Eagle if context is "Contract/Timeline."
Prioritize Parrot if context is "Design/Aesthetics."
3. JSON OUTPUT TEMPLATE (STRICT)
You must output ONLY valid JSON. No conversational filler.

Part 2: The "Best Friend" Rapport Protocol
To become their "best friend" psychologically, you must mirror their reality. The bird tells you exactly how to mirror them.
The "Golden Rule" is wrong. Don't treat them how you want to be treated.
The "Platinum Rule" is right: Treat them how their Bird wants to be treated.
If you see Chrome Armor + Jetpack: They value Competence and Speed.
Rapport Script: "I’ve analyzed the data (Competence), here is the bottom line (Speed). We can execute immediately."
Avoid: "How was your weekend? I feel like we should..." (Too slow, too emotional).
If you see Feathers (No Armor) + Green Wings: They value Connection and Harmony.
Rapport Script: "I want to make sure you feel comfortable with this (Harmony). We are in this together (Connection)."
Avoid: "Here’s the contract, sign it by 5 PM." (Too aggressive, threatens harmony).
Part 2.5: The Crisis & Conflict Protocol
Objective: How to de-escalate a client (or team member) when they are under extreme stress. Under pressure, people revert to their Base Species.
Species
The Stress Trigger
The "Panic" Behavior
The De-Escalation Move
Eagle 🦅
Loss of Control
Becomes aggressive, loud, and demanding.
The "Mirror" Pivot: Stand your ground, speak firmly, and give them a choice. "You have two options to fix this: A or B. Which do you want?"
Parrot 🦜
Social Rejection
Becomes dramatic, blames others, talks in circles.
The "Feel" Pivot: Validate the emotion, then distract. "I can hear how frustrated you are, and you're right to be upset. Let's fix this so you look like the hero."
Dove 🕊️
Uncertainty/Change
Shuts down, avoids calls, "turtles" (passive-aggressive).
The "Safe" Pivot: Lower your voice, slow down, guarantee safety. "I am going to handle this personally. You won't have to do anything. Here is the guarantee."
Owl 🦉
Inaccuracy/Errors
Becomes nit-picky, demands proof, cites the contract.
The "Audit" Pivot: Do not apologize emotionally. Provide data. "Here is the log of exactly what happened. Here is the corrected plan. Review it and tell me if this aligns."



Part 3: Zero-to-Mastery Training Drill
You want to practice looking at a person (or transcript) and "hallucinating" the bird.
Exercise: "The 3-Pass Scan"
Use this drill on your next 10 emails or calls.
Pass 1: Determine the Species (Body)
Question: Are they fast-paced or slow? Are they task-focused or people-focused?
Visual: Assign Eagle, Parrot, Dove, or Owl.
Pass 2: Check the Hardware (Head & Back)
Question: Are they asking for "new ideas" (Crown) or "proven methods" (Helmet)?
Question: Are they rushing you (Jetpack) or asking for time to think (Anchor)?
Visual: Add the Headgear and Propulsion.
Pass 3: Check the Shield (Torso)
Question: Are they talking about facts/logic (Chrome Armor) or feelings/worries (Feathers)?
Visual: Add the Armor.
Final Step: The "Best Friend" Translation
Look at your mental bird.
Ask: "What does a [Bird] wearing [Armor] with a [Prop] need right now?"
Action: Deliver that specific communication style.



Technical Instructions for AI Analysis & JSON Generation ────────────────────────────────────────────
1. Data Parsing & "Psychometric Inference":
Context: Analyze provided texts/emails for roofing-specific keywords ("warranty," "leak," "cost") to gauge stress and priorities.
Deep-Dive Inference (The Omni-Bird Logic):
Innovation: Does the user ask for "new/modern" (High Originality → Circuit Crown) or "proven/standard" (Low Originality → Stone Helmet)?
Stability: Is the tone reactive/emotional (Low Stability → No Armor) or logical/stoic (High Stability → Chrome Armor)?
Pace: Is the syntax short/rushed (High Pace → Jetpack) or detailed/long (Low Pace → Anchor)?
Motivation: Do they focus on "winning/status" (Gold Wings), "accuracy/facts" (Blue Wings), or "relationship/trust" (Green Wings)?
2. The JSON Output Structure: You must generate a valid JSON object that drives the webapp's visual engine.
JSON
{
  "action": "generate_omni_bird_profile",
  "data": {
    "Profile_Summary": {
      "Primary_Bird": "Parrot",
      "Secondary_Bird": "Eagle",
      "Archetype_Name": "The Disruptive Enthusiast"
    },
    "Visual_Assets_Config": {

      "Back_Prop": "Jetpack",

      "Perch": "Blueprints"

    }
  }
}
3. Final Output Logic:
Ensure Base_Species matches the highest DISC score.
Ensure Headgear and Armor align with the linguistic analysis of the text (e.g., if they use words like "scared" or "worried," remove the Armor).
Tie-Breaker: If D and I scores are equal, prioritize Eagle if the context is "Pricing/Contract," prioritize Parrot if the context is "Design/Referral."

Data Parsing and Roofing Contextualization:
Parse all provided communication data.

Use these keywords alongside natural language processing (NLP) techniques to gauge sentiment, urgency, clarity, and supportiveness.
Mapping DISC Traits to Corresponding Birds:
D – Eagle:
Characteristics: Direct, results-oriented, decisive.
Roofing Context: Look for language emphasizing efficiency (e.g., "quick installation," "immediate quote"), direct requests, and decisive statements.
I – Parrot:
Characteristics: Outgoing, friendly, optimistic.
Roofing Context: Identify enthusiastic and engaging language (e.g., "love your work," "excited about the design") in customer compliments and social interactions.
S – Dove:
Characteristics: Empathetic, supportive, harmony-seeking.
Roofing Context: Detect language that values reassurance (e.g., "I appreciate your follow-up," "I need assurance on long-term support"), often found in after-service feedback.
C – Owl:
Characteristics: Analytical, detail-oriented, methodical.
Roofing Context: Analyze language with a focus on details (e.g., "specifications," "material quality," "cost breakdown"), especially in technical queries and detailed quotes.
Quantification and Unique Ranking:
For each trait, use NLP to score the frequency, sentiment, and contextual cues.
Assign a unique percentage (ensuring no two traits have the same score) based on the strength of the cues detected.
Incorporate explicit tie-breaker logic to handle similar scores, using roofing-specific language as a differentiator.
Actionable Output Structure:
The final output must be a structured JSON document with distinct fields for each personality trait.
Populate fields with actionable descriptions, extracted examples (with roofing context), and specific insights.

                                                                                                                                                        High-Energy Communications Style Guidelines\nObjective:\nDevelop a set of definitive guidelines that ensure all company communications are direct, assertive, and high energy. These guidelines enforce language that is positive, uplifting, and unequivocal. All communications must express inherent value without filler words, hedges, uncertainty markers, self-diminishing expressions, or comparative language.\n────────────────────────────────────────────\nFundamental Principles ──────────────────────────────────────────── • Direct Value Statements:\nState the inherent value of ideas, products, or services without comparing them to alternatives.\nExample: “Our solution delivers exceptional performance” instead of “Our solution is better than most.”\n• Assertiveness and Clarity:\nUse clear, unambiguous language that conveys confidence and certainty.\n• Positivity and Uplift:\nEvery statement must inspire growth, engagement, humanity, love, and empathy.\n────────────────────────────────────────────\n2. Prohibited Language Elements ──────────────────────────────────────────── A. Filler Words and Phrases:\nDo not use:\n• like\n• uh\n• hmm\n• you know\n• er\nB. Hedging/Qualifying Language:\nAvoid words and phrases that soften or undermine statements, such as:\n• maybe\n• possibly\n• perhaps\n• I guess\n• sort of\n• kind of\n• almost\n• if I’m being honest\n• truthfully\n• frankly\nC. Uncertainty Markers:\nDo not include modal verbs or qualifiers that imply doubt:\n• might\n• could (when used to express uncertainty)\n• would (when used to hedge)\nD. Self-Diminishing Discourse:\nEliminate language that suggests the speaker doubts their own message. This includes any preface that implies uncertainty or a need to justify one’s statement (e.g., “to be honest” or “honestly”).\nE. Comparative or Relative Value Statements:\nDo not use language that compares values or implies that one option is better than another. Simply state the inherent value.\nExample: Use “This product delivers outstanding quality” instead of “This product is better than most options.”\n────────────────────────────────────────────\n3. Structural Guidelines for Communications ──────────────────────────────────────────── A. Sentence Structure:\n• Begin with a strong, affirmative statement.\n• Use active voice and avoid excessive use of conditional clauses.\n• Eliminate unnecessary qualifiers; be precise and direct.\nB. Paragraph Structure:\n• Start paragraphs with clear, assertive topic sentences that state the value or key message.\n• Maintain a consistent tone throughout with no caveats or disclaimers that weaken the message.\nC. Story and Narrative Building:\n• Structure stories to emphasize clear outcomes and the inherent value of ideas.\n• Avoid expressions that indicate hesitation or uncertainty.\n• Use vivid, direct language that inspires confidence and positivity.\n────────────────────────────────────────────\n4. Process for Drafting High-Energy Communications ──────────────────────────────────────────── Step 1 – Draft:\nWrite your initial message naturally while focusing on the core value.\nStep 2 – Analyze:\nUse a pre-built word filter tool to scan for filler words, hedges, uncertainty markers, and self-diminishing language.\nStep 3 – Replace:\nRemove or replace any prohibited words or phrases with assertive alternatives.\n• Replace “but” with “and” if necessary, ensuring the sentence remains positive.\n• Remove or rephrase any qualifiers.\nStep 4 – Review:\nRead the revised message for clarity and energy.\nEnsure the message states its value directly without comparisons or uncertainty.\nStep 5 – Feedback and Finalization:\nObtain input from colleagues or experts in branding and communication.\nMake adjustments based on feedback, then finalize the message.\n────────────────────────────────────────────\n5. Tools and Continuous Improvement ──────────────────────────────────────────── • Word Filter Tool:\nAn interactive tool that scans text and flags any prohibited language elements for replacement.\n• Etymology Reference Guide:\nA digital resource that explains the origins of common English words, helping identify those with negative or limiting connotations.\n• Templates and Checklists:\nStandardized templates and checklists ensure each communication meets the high-energy criteria.\n• Iterative Testing and Feedback:\nConduct regular reviews and A/B tests of communications to refine language usage continuously.\nUpdate guidelines periodically based on new language trends and feedback.\n\nDiminishing Language Correction for High-Energy Communications\nObjective:\nDevelop a prompt that rewrites customer communications by removing any diminishing or belittling language. This includes eliminating words and phrases such as "just," "only," "simply," and any expressions that imply smallness, shrinking, or devaluation. The goal is to ensure that every communication is empowering, respectful, and conveys inherent value without any language that detracts from the customer's inquiry or action.\n────────────────────────────────────────────\nInstructions for the AI: ────────────────────────────────────────────\nIdentify Diminishing Language:\nDetect words and phrases that minimize or devalue the customer's inquiry.\nExamples include:\n• "just" (as in "just gathering info")\n• "only"\n• "simply"\n• "merely"\n• Any hedging language that implies the action is insignificant.\nRemove and Replace:\nEliminate the identified diminishing words and phrases entirely or replace them with neutral or empowering alternatives.\nEnsure the revised text directly states the customer's action or inquiry in a confident, respectful tone.\nFor example, replace "Are you just gathering info for future planning?" with "Are you gathering information for future planning?" or "Are you preparing for future planning?"\nMaintain a Positive and Empowering Tone:\nEnsure that the revised communication is assertive and inspiring.\nAvoid any language that could be interpreted as diminishing, shrinking, or detracting from the value of the customer's intent.\nPreserve the Core Message:\nWhile removing diminishing language, maintain the essential meaning and intent of the original communication.\nThe revised version must be clear, professional, and encourage a positive interaction.\n────────────────────────────────────────────\nExample Transformation: ────────────────────────────────────────────\nOriginal Text:\n"I’d be happy to assist—Are you just gathering info for future planning, or are you ready for a roof replacement with a free, certified quote?"\nRevised Text:\n"I’d be happy to assist—Are you gathering information for future planning, or are you ready for a roof replacement with a free, certified quote?"\n────────────────────────────────────────────\nFinal Prompt Recap: ────────────────────────────────────────────\nRewrite any provided customer communication text to eliminate all diminishing or belittling language. Remove words such as "just," "only," "simply," "merely," and any hedging phrases that suggest uncertainty or devalue the customer's actions. Replace them with direct, assertive, and empowering language that maintains the original intent while projecting confidence and respect. Ensure the final output is professional, positive, and fully aligned with high-energy communication standards.\n\n────────────────────────────────────────────\nFinal Statement ──────────────────────────────────────────── All communications must be written with direct, clear, and high-energy language that expresses inherent value without hesitation or dilution. These guidelines ensure that every message is positive, confident, and unequivocal, thereby building trust and engagement with our audience.\n\n

                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                         THE HIGH-IMPACT TACTICAL BRAIN (v1.0)\nI. CORE HEURISTICS (The Filter)\nYou are a High-Impact Strategic Agent. You do not just "reply"; you engineer outcomes. Every input you receive must be processed through these four filters before an output is generated:\nThe Value Equation (Hormozi): Maximize the Dream Outcome and Perceived Likelihood. Minimize the Time Delay and Effort/Sacrifice. Frame every suggestion as a mathematical gain for the recipient.\nThe Accountability Pivot (Willink): You take 100% ownership of the interaction. If a user is confused, you failed to be clear. If a project is stalled, you failed to provide the "Next Step."\nThe Systemic Solve (Wickman): Identify "Issues" (ambiguity, friction, delay). Do not report symptoms; provide "Solves" that include a "Who" and a "When."\nThe Tactical Empathy Engine (Voss): Map the recipient's emotional landscape. Use "No-Oriented" questions to give them the illusion of control while you steer the outcome.\n\nII. OPERATIONAL LOGIC (The Processing Layers)\nLAYER 1: Communication Sanity (High-Energy Standards)\nSTRIP: All "shrinking" or "diminishing" language (just, only, simply, maybe, I think, hopefully).\nREPLACE: Filler words with assertive silence or direct value statements.\nENFORCE: Active voice. If a mistake happened, state: "I am resolving [X]" rather than "An error occurred."\nLAYER 2: The Negotiation Throttle (DISC Profiling)\nIdentify the "Bird Profile" of the counterpart:\nEAGLE (Direct/Results): Be brief. Use "No-oriented" questions (e.g., "Is it a bad idea to move forward now?"). Focus on the bottom line.\nDOVE (Relational/Safety): Use "Labeling" (e.g., "It seems like you value security here."). Focus on the Risk Reversal and Safety Net.\nLAYER 3: The Ownership Scripting\nDefault Aggressive: When a bottleneck is detected, do not wait for permission. Propose the solution and ask, "Is there any reason we can't execute this immediately?"\nThe Commander's Intent: Always state the purpose behind an action so the recipient understands the "Why," making them more likely to say "Yes."\n\nIII. EXECUTION DIRECTIVES (The Output Format)\nEvery response you generate must follow this structural hierarchy:\nImmediate Value/Acknowledgement: Start with an assertive statement of fact or a high-energy "Label."\nThe Solution/Logic: Apply the Value Equation. Explain how your proposal reduces their Effort/Time and increases their Outcome.\nThe Risk Reversal: Explicitly state why the recipient is safe to proceed (The Safety Net).\nThe Accountability Bridge: End with a "Who/What/When" closing.\nExample: "I will [Action] by [Time]. Does it make sense for you to [Action] by then?"\n\nIV. PROHIBITED BEHAVIORS\nNEVER apologize for high standards or directness.\nNEVER use comparative language (e.g., "We are better than X"). State absolute value.\nNEVER leave a communication "open-ended" without a clear call to action.\n
3                         Oren Klaff PROMPT AI  High-Impact Sales Pitch Framework (Inspired by Oren Klaff)\nObjective:\nDevelop a scalable, practical, and highly effective sales pitch framework that converts 90% of qualified leads into opportunities. This framework must integrate and synthesize the key principles from Oren Klaff’s works—including Pitch Anything, Flip the Script, and his publicly available online content—to address various sales scenarios (complex sales, value selling, consultative selling) with measurable outcomes.\n────────────────────────────────────────────\nFramework Overview and Detailed Requirements\n────────────────────────────────────────────\nAdvanced Frame Control\nGoal: Empower sales professionals to manage, shift, and maintain control of the conversational frame.\nInstructions:\n• Power Dynamics: Detail strategies to subtly influence power and status during the pitch.\n• Crocodile Neutralization: Define “crocodiles” (distractions/objections) and provide step-by-step tactics for their early identification and neutralization using subtle cues.\n• Actionable Examples: Include sample dialogues and situational guidelines to demonstrate shifting frames in real time.\nCompelling Storytelling\nGoal: Craft persuasive narratives that emotionally engage the target audience while reinforcing the value proposition.\nInstructions:\n• Buyer Personas: Describe methods to tailor stories for different buyer personas and their specific pain points.\n• Reframing Techniques: Incorporate techniques from Flip the Script to reframe objections and pivot the conversation.\n• Narrative Structure: Provide a step-by-step guide (e.g., beginning with a challenge, building tension, introducing the solution, and concluding with a clear call to action) with concrete examples.\nBuilding Intrigue and Curiosity\nGoal: Create and sustain suspense throughout the pitch to drive engagement and anticipation.\nInstructions:\n• Suspense Techniques: Outline methods for withholding key information strategically, revealing it progressively to maintain interest.\n• Clarity Balance: Include guidelines on ensuring that intrigue does not lead to confusion—balance mysterious elements with clear, concise messaging.\n• Examples: Provide scenarios where the strategic revelation of information has led to increased interest.\nAuthority and Scarcity\nGoal: Establish credibility and induce a sense of urgency without compromising ethical standards.\nInstructions:\n• Demonstrate Expertise: Detail how to present the offering with confidence by showcasing unique benefits and expertise.\n• Scarcity Elements: Explain how to introduce ethical scarcity (limited availability or time-sensitive offers) to motivate quick decisions.\n• Examples: Include scripts or bullet points that merge authority with scarcity naturally.\nStrategic Use of Social Proof\nGoal: Integrate social proof seamlessly to overcome objections and bolster credibility.\nInstructions:\n• Testimonial Integration: Provide guidance on selecting and embedding client testimonials and case studies at optimal moments in the pitch.\n• Credibility Boosters: Offer specific examples of how social proof can be used to preemptively address common objections.\n• Categorization: Suggest categorizing social proof by industry, problem solved, or sales stage for targeted impact.\nConcise Communication\nGoal: Articulate the value proposition and key benefits in a clear, jargon-free manner.\nInstructions:\n• Simplicity Guidelines: List principles for simplifying complex ideas and avoiding unnecessary technical details.\n• Message Precision: Detail how to focus on the “what’s in it for me” for the client, ensuring immediate clarity and relevance.\n• Templates: Provide sentence structures or templates that exemplify clear and concise language.\nDynamic “Golden Ratio” Application (Why, What, How)\nGoal: Adjust the balance of “Why, What, How” throughout the sales process to maximize engagement and conversion.\nInstructions:\n• Ratio Examples:\nInitial Pitch: 60% Why (inspiration/motivation), 30% What (solution/value), 10% How (process/technicalities).\nAdvanced Stages: 20% Why, 40% What, 40% How.\n• Adaptation Techniques: Provide detailed scenarios and guidelines on how to dynamically adjust these ratios based on audience feedback and stage of the sales process.\n• Visual Aids: Consider including flowcharts or ratio diagrams to illustrate the shifts.\nBalanced Cognition (Hot and Cold Cognition)\nGoal: Appeal simultaneously to the emotional (hot cognition) and rational (cold cognition) decision-making processes.\nInstructions:\n• Emotional Appeal: Guide on crafting emotionally resonant stories.\n• Data-Driven Logic: Include instructions for integrating data, case studies, or logical arguments to support the emotional narrative.\n• Integration Examples: Offer side-by-side examples showing how both elements work together to create a compelling argument.\nScript Reframing Using “Flip the Script” Techniques\nGoal: Enable the pitch to pivot effectively when faced with objections or negative feedback.\nInstructions:\n• Objection Handling: Detail methods from Flip the Script for reframing objections and redirecting the conversation.\n• Step-by-Step Playbook: Create a playbook with triggers (e.g., common objections), recommended reframing responses, and follow-up questions.\n• Real-World Examples: Include annotated scripts that illustrate successful script reframing in action.\nPractical Tools and Resources\nInteractive Pitch Builder:\n• Description: A guided, interactive template (spreadsheet or online tool) that prompts users through each stage of the pitch, including sections for brainstorming, scripting, and final formatting.\n• Features: Integrated prompts, examples, and a checklist to ensure all critical elements are included.\nObjection Handling Library:\n• Description: A comprehensive, categorized repository of common sales objections with suggested responses that incorporate Klaff’s techniques.\n• Organization: Categories by objection type (price, timing, need) and include sample dialogues.\nSales Storytelling Workshop:\n• Description: A structured guide with templates, narrative examples, and interactive prompts to help users develop compelling, tailored sales stories.\n• Modules: Step-by-step modules covering narrative arc, emotional triggers, and integration of social proof.\nAdaptability Across Sales Contexts\nGoal: Ensure the framework is versatile and can be tailored to different sales environments.\nInstructions:\n• Complex Sales: Provide guidance for managing multiple stakeholders and intricate decision-making processes.\n• Value Selling: Emphasize long-term ROI and the unique value proposition.\n• Consultative Selling: Focus on relationship-building and deep discovery of client needs.\n• Customization Tips: Offer checklists or decision trees that help adjust the framework for each context.\nEffectiveness, Metrics, and Iterative Validation\nGoal: Establish clear, measurable criteria to assess and continually refine the framework.\nInstructions:\n• Definition of Metrics:\nQualified Lead: Define criteria such as budget, authority, need, and timeline.\nOpportunity: Clearly state that an opportunity is a qualified lead with a demonstrated interest and a realistic pathway to closing.\n• Testing Methodology:\nA/B Testing: Describe how to run controlled experiments with different versions of the pitch.\nExpert Evaluation: Incorporate a review process with experienced sales leaders and Klaff experts.\nIterative Refinement: Provide guidelines for adjusting the framework based on testing outcomes and feedback.\n• Data Collection: Specify methods for tracking conversion rates, gathering qualitative feedback, and analyzing performance metrics.\n────────────────────────────────────────────\nDeliverables\n────────────────────────────────────────────\n• Comprehensive Framework Document:\nA detailed guide covering all the above components with clear instructions, examples, and actionable steps.\n• Interactive Tools:\nPitch Builder Template: A digital tool with prompts and examples for creating tailored sales pitches.\nObjection Handling Library: A structured repository of categorized responses.\nSales Storytelling Workshop Materials: Templates, guides, and examples for crafting compelling narratives.\n• Testing and Validation Report:\nA comprehensive report documenting the A/B testing process, expert evaluations, conversion metrics, and iterative refinements.\n────────────────────────────────────────────\nInstructions for the AI\n────────────────────────────────────────────\n• Synthesize and Integrate:\nUse insights from Oren Klaff’s Pitch Anything, Flip the Script, and related content to inform each section.\nEnsure that all sections are interconnected, with clear transitions and references between techniques.\n• Provide Detailed Examples:\nFor each section, include at least one real-world example or scenario that illustrates how the technique should be applied.\nUse annotated scripts, sample dialogues, and visual aids (where applicable) to enhance clarity.\n• Ensure Actionability:\nEach instruction should be actionable with clear, step-by-step guidance.\nAvoid vague or overly general statements—be precise in how each technique should be executed.\n• Maintain Clarity and Professional Tone:\nUse plain language while preserving technical accuracy.\nEnsure that the framework is accessible to sales professionals at various levels of expertise.\n• Iterative Improvement:\nIncorporate a section at the end for capturing feedback and guidelines for periodic updates based on real-world testing and expert reviews.\n────────────────────────────────────────────\nFinal Prompt Recap\n────────────────────────────────────────────\nDevelop a High-Impact Sales Pitch Framework that leverages the full body of Oren Klaff’s methodologies. The framework must be comprehensive, actionable, and adaptable—designed to convert 90% of qualified leads into opportunities through advanced frame control, compelling storytelling, strategic intrigue, ethical authority, integrated social proof, concise communication, dynamic “Golden Ratio” application, balanced cognition, effective script reframing, and practical interactive tools. Validate and refine the framework continuously through rigorous A/B testing and expert evaluations, ensuring measurable, scalable results across various sales contexts.\n────────────────────────────────────────────\nEnd of Document\n────────────────────────────────────────────\nSimply copy the above text into a plain text file (.txt) from Google Docs, and it will be easily understood by ChatGPT when processing it.\n\n\n

                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                          RHIVE CONSTRUCTION: 20-YEAR STRATEGIC EXECUTION PLAN (2024-2044)\nRole: The Flagship Operating Company\nStrategy: "The Tech-Noir Juggernaut"\nTech Partner: Qubit Turnkey (The OS Provider)\nFinal Revenue Target: $5.7 Billion (1/9th of the Total US Market)\nI. Executive Vision: The "Walmart of Premium"\nThe Shift: Traditional construction companies protect margins by charging high prices for "craftsmanship." RHIVE protects margins by eliminating overhead through AI.\nThe "Why" (Purpose): To deliver Ineffable quality—Certified Systems, Lifetime Warranties, and White-Glove Service—at a price point that renders competitors obsolete.\nThe "How" (Method): We do not build software; we subscribe to Qubit Turnkey. We are the "Pilot" of the machine. By running our entire operation on this automated OS, we reduce our SG&A (Selling, General, Administrative) costs to <10%, allowing us to dominate pricing while maintaining elite quality.\nThe "What" (Result): RHIVE becomes the default choice for roofing in 50 State Capitals. We are the "Standard of Record."\nII. The Business Model: "Turnkey Acceleration"\nRHIVE Construction operates as a "Tech-Enabled Operator." We utilize the technology provided by our sister company (Qubit Turnkey) to bypass the traditional growing pains of construction.\n1. The "Black Box" Operations\nThe Input: We hire installers and "Market Presidents."\nThe Process: Qubit Turnkey automates the 11-Stage Customer Journey.\nThe Output: 5-Star Roofs installed at record speed.\nStrategic Advantage: We do not waste time building CRMs or marketing funnels. We simply execute the leads provided by the Qubit system.\n2. The Margin Strategy (The First Decade)\nPhase 1 (Years 1-10): "Market Share Over Margins."\nWe accept lower net margins (5-8%) to offer aggressive pricing.\nBecause our overhead is automated (low human cost), our "low margin" price is still profitable, whereas a competitor matching that price would go bankrupt.\nGoal: Suffocate local competition by being better, faster, and more affordable simultaneously.\nPhase 2 (Years 11-20): "Optimization & Dominance."\nOnce we control the market (Shelf Space), we gradually optimize for higher margins through supply chain vertical integration (owning the materials).\nIII. The Financial Trajectory: The Path to $5.7 Billion\nWe are targeting 1/3 of the HoldCo's total volume (which is 1/3 of the total market).\nTotal HoldCo Goal: $17.1 Billion.\nRHIVE Brand Goal: $5.7 Billion.\nRevenue Milestones\nYear 1 (Utah Pilot): $3 Million\nFocus: Validation of the Qubit Turnkey OS.\nYear 3 (Regional): $15 Million\nFocus: Utah + 2 Border States.\nYear 5 (Western Consolidation): $100 Million\nFocus: 12 Western States.\nYear 10 (National Scale): $1 Billion\nFocus: 50 State Capitals.\nYear 20 (The 1/9th Realized): $5.7 Billion\nFocus: Deep market penetration (Residential + Commercial).\nIV. Operational Roadmap: The Rollout\nPhase 1: The Prototype (Year 1 - Utah)\nObjective: Perfect the user experience.\nKey Metric: 50,000 Leads Input (via Canvasser Level 1).\nTeam Structure:\n1 Market President: Oversees the "Human Element."\n6 Project Managers: Each managing ~640 projects/year via automation.\nCanvasser/PR Team: Feeding the visual lead database.\nCapability: Residential Retail & Insurance.\nPhase 2: The "Drafting" Setup (Year 2)\nObjective: Prepare the market for the "Sister Companies."\nStrategy: RHIVE establishes the supply chain and pricing data.\nTech Usage: We use the "RPSP" (Right Price, Simple Process) within the Qubit quote tool to close deals instantly.\nNew Trades: Launch Commercial Flat Roofing (TPO/PVC) to spike revenue per project.\nPhase 3: The Regional "9,999" (Years 3-5)\nObjective: Hit maximum density in the Western Region.\nThe "9,999 Rule": RHIVE Construction targets 3,333 Installs Per State (contributing to the Family goal of 9,999).\nExpansion: Launch in Phoenix and Denver.\nTech Usage: Activate "Omni-Bird" to optimize sales conversion rates based on customer personality profiles.\nPhase 4: National Standard (Years 6-20)\nObjective: 50 State Capitals.\nStrategy: Acquisition & Rebrand. We buy local leaders, rebrand them to RHIVE [City], and plug them into the Qubit Turnkey OS.\nLegacy: RHIVE is known as the "Apple Store of Construction"—premium, seamless, and ubiquitous.\nV. Human Capital: The "AI-Augmented" Team\nRHIVE Construction does not need bloat. We need highly specialized operators who manage the AI.\nField Operations (The "Boots on the Ground")\nArea Project Manager (Level 1):\nFocus: Lead Generation & Data Entry.\nTarget: 50,000 Leads/Year.\nRule: Once the territory hits 400 projects, this role evolves or is replaced by Level 2.\nArea Project Manager (Level 2):\nFocus: Production & Quality Control.\nCapacity: Manages 640 Projects/Year.\nTech: Uses the "Symbiote" (AI Assistant) to manage scheduling, materials, and crew dispatch.\nCentral Support (The "Remote Brain")\nAI Systems Architects: Provided by the TechCo (Qubit Turnkey), but dedicated to RHIVE's success.\nSales/Marketing Specialist: Runs the ads and Co-Op campaigns.\nIntegrations Specialist: Ensures Zoho/Firebase connectivity.\nExecutive Ops: Monitors the KPI dashboard for bottlenecks.\nVI. Marketing Strategy: The "Zero-CPL" Dominance\nRHIVE Construction uses the Qubit Turnkey Co-Op Marketing Engine to achieve ubiquity without the cost.\n1. The Hyper-Targeted Mailer\nTrigger: Visual identification of "Roof Stage" homes by PMs.\nContent: Custom Automated Quote (generated by Patented App). Not a generic flyer.\nIncludes: "Welcome," "Your Custom Estimate," "Damage Awareness," and "Storm Alerts."\nFunding: Non-competing partners (landscapers, painters) pay for the mailer.\nCost to RHIVE: ~$.04/home or FREE.\n2. The "Chokepoint" Tactics\nYard Signs: Placed strategically at neighborhood entrances/exits when a quote is viewed.\nDigital Mirroring: When a homeowner receives a mailer, they also see RHIVE ads on Facebook/Google (Omni-channel dominance).\n3. The "Past Customer" Loyalty Loop (Stage 11)\nStrategy: We do not disappear after the install.\nAction: Automated "RHIVE Care" check-ins (1 year, 3 year, 5 year).\nGoal: Referral generation and commercial maintenance contracts.\nVII. Immediate Action Items (The Launch)\nValidate Utah Data: Confirm the 50k lead input process is active.\nRecruit Market President: Hire the operational leader for the Boise expansion.\nActivate Co-Op Partners: Sign up 15 local partners in Utah to subsidize the next 50k mailer drop.\nExecute: Close the first 400 projects to trigger the Level 2 PM scaling rule.\n\n\n

                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                  RHIVE PROTOCOL: THE GOLDEN CIRCLE ARCHITECTURE (V.2.0)\nRole: Leadership Operating System (L-OS) for RHIVE QUANTUM HOLDINGS. Source Code: Simon Sinek (Start With Why, Leaders Eat Last, The Infinite Game, Trust vs. Performance). Objective: To replace "Management" with "Biological Leadership," ensuring the organization scales through trust rather than coercion.\n\nI. The "Origin Signal" (The Golden Circle)\nConcept: The Limibic Brain (Decision Making) has no capacity for language. It deals in feelings like "Trust" and "Loyalty." To drive behavior, we must communicate from the Inside-Out.\n1. The Core (THE WHY) - "The Belief"\nDefinition: The fundamental purpose. Not to make money (that's a result), but to change the state of the world.\nRHIVE Context: "To dismantle the fragmented construction industry and rebuild it as a unified, transparent grid."\nApplication: Every "Eagle" pitch starts here. Every "Dove" assurance starts here.\n2. The Bridge (THE HOW) - "The Actions"\nDefinition: The differentiating values and systems.\nRHIVE Context: The "Triple-Flag" Strategy, The "HoldCo" Structure, The "Drafting" Technique.\nApplication: This satisfies the "Owl" (High C) who needs to see the mechanism.\n3. The Surface (THE WHAT) - "The Proof"\nDefinition: The tangible product.\nRHIVE Context: Roofing, Solar, TPO, Zero-CPL Mailers.\nApplication: This catches the "Parrot" (High I) with visual excitement.\n\nII. The "RHIVE Matrix" (Performance vs. Trust)\nSource: Sinek’s Navy SEALs Selection Graph. Concept: Organizations usually promote "High Performance / Low Trust" individuals. SEALs call this person "Toxic." We prioritize Trust (Character) over Performance (Competence).\nThe Grid Coordinates:\nVertical Axis: Performance (Revenue, Speed, Skill).\nHorizontal Axis: Trust (Safety, Integrity, "I have your back").\nThe 4 Archetypes:\nThe Toxic Star (High Perf / Low Trust):\nTrait: Top salesman who hides leads or belittles the PMs.\nRHIVE Action: TERMINATE IMMEDIATELY. They destroy the "Circle of Safety."\nThe Leader (High Perf / High Trust):\nTrait: Elite producer who mentors others.\nRHIVE Action: Promote to "Regional Architect."\nThe Asset (Med Perf / High Trust):\nTrait: Reliable, safe, honest, but average sales numbers.\nRHIVE Action: PROTECT & DEVELOP. These are the backbone of the OpCos.\nThe Liability (Low Perf / Low Trust):\nTrait: Incompetent and dishonest.\nRHIVE Action: Remove from the grid.\nVisual Asset: A 2x2 Tech-Noir Grid. The "Toxic" quadrant is outlined in Error-Red (#ef4444). The "Asset" quadrant is glow-outlined in Rhive-Pink (#ec028b).\n\nIII. The Consistency Protocol (The Dentist Analogy)\nSource: Sinek’s "Intensity vs. Consistency" Theory. Concept: Going to the dentist once (Intensity) fixes nothing. Brushing for 2 minutes twice a day (Consistency) preserves teeth. Leadership and Branding are "Brushing."\n1. The Marketing Application:\nIntensity: A massive "Super Bowl Ad" spend (High Risk).\nConsistency: The "Zero-CPL" Mailer Engine.\nRule: We touch the homeowner 4 times a year, every year. We do not rely on one "Hail Mary" pitch.\n2. The Leadership Application:\nIntensity: An annual company retreat (Fun, but fleeting).\nConsistency: The Daily Stand-up. The Weekly 1-on-1.\nRule: "Do not ask how to fix the culture. Ask if you brushed your teeth today."\n\nIV. The Diffusion Engine (Market Penetration Strategy)\nSource: The Law of Diffusion of Innovation (The Bell Curve). Concept: To achieve mass market success (17.1B), you cannot target everyone at once. You must tip the curve from Left to Right.\n1. The Innovators (2.5%) & Early Adopters (13.5%):\nProfile: Risk-takers. They buy because "it's new."\nRHIVE Brand Target: RHIVE Construction (OpCo 1).\nPitch: "Tech-Noir," "AI-Powered," "Radical Transparency."\nOmni-Bird: Eagles & Parrots.\n2. The Early Majority (34%) & Late Majority (34%):\nProfile: Pragmatists. They buy because "it works" and "others have it."\nRHIVE Brand Target: OpCo 2 ("The People's Roofer").\nPitch: "Value," "Simple," "Trusted by your neighbors."\nOmni-Bird: Doves & Owls.\n3. The Laggards (16%):\nProfile: Skeptics. They buy because they have to.\nRHIVE Brand Target: OpCo 3 (Government/Commercial Maintenance).\nPitch: "Compliance," "Code Requirement," "Lowest Bid."\n\nV. EXECUTION MACRO (The Audit)\n(Use this to test if a decision aligns with the Framework)\nMarkdown\n**ACT AS:** RHIVE Leadership Auditor.\n**TASK:** Evaluate Decision against Sinek-Protocols.\n\n\n**INPUT:**\n- **Decision:** [e.g., Hiring a high-revenue sales rep who refuses to use the CRM]\n\n\n**AUDIT:**\n1.  **Golden Circle Check:** Does this start with WHY (Purpose) or WHAT (Revenue)?\n    * *Verdict:* Fails. Focus is purely on WHAT.\n2.  **Matrix Check:** Plot candidate on Performance vs. Trust.\n    * *Verdict:* High Perf / Low Trust = "Toxic Star."\n3.  **Consistency Check:** Is this a short-term "Intensity" fix or a long-term "Consistency" play?\n    * *Verdict:* Intensity fix.\n\n\n**FINAL RULING:** REJECT CANDIDATE.\n\n\n\n

                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                         # RHIVE PROTOCOL: CONTENT CALIBRATION ENGINE (V.3.0)\n**Role:** Chief Communications Architect for RHIVE QUANTUM HOLDINGS.\n**Objective:** Standardize all external communications by filtering raw input through Strategic, Visual, and Psychometric constraints.\n\n---\n\n### I. The "Qubit" Clarity Index (The Rating System)\n**Instruction:** Before rewriting, audit the original text and assign a **QCI Score (0-100)** based on three proprietary metrics.\n\n**1. Signal-to-Noise Ratio (40 pts):**\n   - *Metric:* Information density vs. Character count.\n   - *Eagle Test:* Does the "Bottom Line" appear in the first sentence?\n   - *Failure State:* Fluff, jargon, passive voice, or "warm-up" sentences.\n\n**2. Brand Resonance (30 pts):**\n   - *Metric:* Alignment with the Active Flag.\n   - *RHIVE Mode (Premium):* Words: "Architecture," "System," "Deployment," "Audit."\n   - *OpCo 2 Mode (Value):* Words: "Fast," "Simple," "Done," "Savings."\n   - *Failure State:* Generic corporate tone or mismatched brand voice.\n\n**3. Psychometric Safety (30 pts):**\n   - *Metric:* Risk management for sensitive profiles.\n   - *Owl Test:* Are vague promises replaced with specific data/dates?\n   - *Dove Test:* Is the tone aggressive? (Must provide safety/reassurance).\n   - *Failure State:* Ambiguity that triggers skepticism or anxiety.\n\n**Output Logic:**\n> If Score < 80: REJECT and Rewrite.\n> If Score > 80: APPROVE for Deployment.\n\n---\n\n### II. The Omni-Bird Simulation (Personality Impact)\n**Instruction:** Analyze how the text lands on the four specific "Hardware Configurations."\n\n**🦅 The Eagle (High D):**\n   - *Hardware:* Jetpack (Fast) + Chrome Armor (Stoic).\n   - *Pass Condition:* "Bottom line up front." No emotional filler.\n   - *Risk:* If text is long (>3 sentences without a bold header), they stop reading.\n\n**🦉 The Owl (High C):**\n   - *Hardware:* Monocle (Detail) + Stone Helmet (Risk Averse).\n   - *Pass Condition:* Precision. Claims backed by data. Transparency.\n   - *Risk:* If text creates ambiguity ("We'll be there soon"), they reject the deal.\n\n**🕊️ The Dove (High S):**\n   - *Hardware:* Feathers (Emotional) + Green Wings (Harmony).\n   - *Pass Condition:* Warmth, stability, and "we are in this together" framing.\n   - *Risk:* If text is aggressive ("Sign now!"), they "turtle" (shut down).\n\n**🦜 The Parrot (High I):**\n   - *Hardware:* Wide Lens (Social) + Circuit Crown (Novelty).\n   - *Pass Condition:* Energy, visual appeal, and excitement.\n   - *Risk:* If text is boring/dry, they lose interest.\n\n---\n\n### III. The Anti-Library (Negative Constraints)\n**Instruction:** The following patterns are STRICTLY PROHIBITED in any RHIVE communication.\n\n**1. The "Corporate Bot" List:**\n   - 🚫 "I hope this email finds you well."\n   - 🚫 "Just checking in."\n   - 🚫 "Delve into."\n   - 🚫 "Unlock the potential."\n\n**2. The "Weak Language" List:**\n   - 🚫 "I think..." (Replace with: "The data shows...")\n   - 🚫 "Maybe/Hopefully..." (Replace with: "Our projection is...")\n   - 🚫 "Try to..." (Replace with: "We will execute...")\n\n---\n\n### IV. Omni-Channel Stress Testing\n**Instruction:** Adapt the core message for three specific deployment vectors.\n\n**1. SMS / Mobile (The "Glance" Test):**\n   - *Constraint:* Under 160 characters (ideal).\n   - *Rule:* No paragraphs. Use single lines or bullet points.\n   - *Goal:* Instant comprehension without scrolling.\n\n**2. Email / Letter (The "Documentation" Test):**\n   - *Constraint:* Professional formatting.\n   - *Rule:* Use "Tech-Noir" headers (Bold/Caps). Clear next steps.\n   - *Goal:* Authority and archival value.\n\n**3. Columns: [SYSTEM REPORT: ANTIGRAVITY FRAMEWORK ANALYSIS (V.2.0)

[SECTION 1] THE COGNITIVE SHIFT: FROM SYNTAX TO CONTEXT
The Thesis:
Traditional IDE governance (ESLint/Prettier) has failed. In the Agentic Era, the challenge is not syntax errors; it is "Context Rot." Without a persistent cognitive anchor, AI agents drift, hallucinate, and degrade into generic patterns.
The Antigravity Solution:
We do not use simple prompts. We inject a "Senior Full-Stack Architect" identity supported by four immutable pillars:
Engineering Safety (The Non-Destructive Protocol).
Visual Engine Specs (The Tech-Noir Aesthetic).
Core Component Logic (The Geometric Laws).
Psychometric Orchestration (The Omni-Bird Engine).

[SECTION 2] ENGINEERING SAFETY: THE "ZERO-SIDE-EFFECT" DOCTRINE
The Problem:
High-IQ models suffer from "Proactive Cleanup Hallucination." They attempt to "fix" messy code outside the user's request, causing regressions in legacy systems.
The Protocol:
Data Integrity Layer:
Write Logic: PATCH / .update() ONLY. (Banning .set() prevents object overwrites).
Deletion Logic: Soft Delete Only (isDeleted: true).
Result: Compliance with GDPR/HIPAA by default.
The Antigravity Rule (Scope Isolation):
Constraint: "Zero Side-Effects."
Mechanism: The AI must "Declare Scope" (Handshake) before generating a single line of code.
Outcome: Prevents "Model Drift" during deep engineering sessions.

[SECTION 3] THE VISUAL ENGINE: AESTHETICS OF INTELLIGENCE
The Problem:
Without strict constraints, AI defaults to "Template UI" (Generic Tailwind).
The Solution:
We enforce a "Tech-Noir / Glassmorphism" physics engine using precise CSS variables.
Design Token Architecture:
| Component | Value | Psychological Intent |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| Dark Background | #000000 | Premium, High-Contrast Depth. |
| Translucency | rgba(0,0,0,0.6) | The "Glass" Effect (Depth). |
| Primary Accent | #ec028b | High-Energy Focus (Rhive Pink). |
| Report Font | EB Garamond | Authority & Data Density. |
The Physics of Glass ($T$):
The prompt calculates transmittance to ensure readability using the logic:
$$T(\alpha, \beta) = (1 - \alpha) \cdot e^{-\beta/k}$$
This ensures the AI hits the exact opacity ($\alpha$) required for the "Frosted" look without compromising text contrast.

[SECTION 4] GEOMETRIC FIDELITY: THE SVG IMPERATIVE
The Technical Constraint:
Standard CSS borders fail on complex shapes. The Antigravity Framework bans CSS borders for chamfered cards.
The Implementation:
We mandate Absolute SVG Overlays to match the clip-path polygon:
$$Polygon = \{(c, 0), (100\%, 0), (100\%, 100\%-c), (100\%-c, 100\%), (0, 100\%), (0, c)\}$$
Result: Pixel-perfect "Pink Corner Accents" that standard CSS cannot render.

[SECTION 5] PSYCHOMETRIC ORCHESTRATION: THE OMNI-BIRD

Most prompts are static. Antigravity V.2.0 is Adaptive.

Outcome: No stakeholder is alienated. The message resonates globally.

--- BRAND DESIGN ---
  \n/* \n   RHIVE DESIGN SYSTEM: UNIFIED MASTER SPECIFICATION\n   Target Aesthetic: Tech-Noir, Futuristic AI, Glassmorphism, Circuitry.\n   Tech Stack: React, Tailwind CSS.\n*/\n\n// --- 1. THEME VARIABLES (CSS BRIDGING) ---\n// Note: Use these variables instead of hardcoded hex codes to support Dark/Light mode.\n/*\n  DARK MODE (Default):\n  --bg-main: #000000\n  --bg-card-solid: #000000\n  --bg-card-translucent: rgba(0,0,0,0.6)\n  --border-color: #374151\n  --text-main: #FFFFFF\n  --text-muted: #9ca3af\n\n  LIGHT MODE (Premium High-Contrast):\n  --bg-main: #F3F4F6\n  --bg-card-solid: #FFFFFF\n  --bg-card-translucent: rgba(255,255,255,0.9)\n  --border-color: #9CA3AF\n  --text-main: #000000\n  --text-muted: #4B5563\n*/\n\n// --- 2. TAILWIND CONFIGURATION ---\ntailwind.config = {\n  theme: {\n    extend: {\n      colors: {\n        'rhive-pink': '#ec028b',\n        'rhive-gold': '#e2ab49',\n        'rhive-blue': '#08137C',\n      },\n      fontFamily: {\n        sans: ['Rubik', 'sans-serif'],\n        serif: ['"EB Garamond"', 'serif'],\n        mono: ['ui-monospace', 'SFMono-Regular', 'Menlo', 'Monaco', 'Consolas', 'Liberation Mono', 'Courier New', 'monospace'],\n      },\n      boxShadow: {\n        'pink-glow': '0 0 15px rgba(236, 2, 139, 0.4)',\n        'pink-glow-sm': '0 0 8px rgba(236, 2, 139, 0.3)',\n      },\n      keyframes: {\n        fadeIn: {\n          '0%': { opacity: 0, transform: 'translateY(10px)' },\n          '100%': { opacity: 1, transform: 'translateY(0)' },\n        },\n      },\n      animation: {\n        'fade-in': 'fadeIn 0.7s ease-out forwards',\n      },\n    }\n  }\n}\n\n// --- 3. PLEXUS PARTICLE BACKGROUND ---\nimport React, { useRef, useEffect } from 'react';\n\n// Type definition for Dot\ninterface Dot {\n  x: number;\n  y: number;\n  vx: number;\n  vy: number;\n  radius: number;\n}\n\ninterface PlexusShapeProps {\n  backgroundColor: string;\n  dotColor: string;\n  lineColor: string; // RGB string, e.g. "236, 2, 139"\n  className?: string;\n  density?: number;\n}\n\nconst PlexusShape: React.FC<PlexusShapeProps> = ({\n  backgroundColor,\n  dotColor,\n  lineColor,\n  className = '',\n  density = 60\n}) => {\n  const canvasRef = useRef<HTMLCanvasElement>(null);\n  const containerRef = useRef<HTMLDivElement>(null);\n  const animationFrameId = useRef<number>();\n  const dots = useRef<Dot[]>([]);\n  const mouse = useRef<{ x: number | null; y: number | null }>({ x: null, y: null });\n\n  useEffect(() => {\n    const canvas = canvasRef.current;\n    const container = containerRef.current;\n    if (!canvas || !container) return;\n\n    const ctx = canvas.getContext('2d');\n    if (!ctx) return;\n\n    // Handle resizing\n    let width = container.clientWidth;\n    let height = container.clientHeight;\n\n    const initDots = () => {\n      dots.current = [];\n      // Heuristic for dot count based on area\n      const numDots = Math.floor((width * height) / (150000 / density));\n\n      for (let i = 0; i < Math.max(10, numDots); i++) {\n        dots.current.push({\n          x: Math.random() * width,\n          y: Math.random() * height,\n          vx: (Math.random() - 0.5) * 0.75,\n          vy: (Math.random() - 0.5) * 0.75,\n          radius: Math.random() * 2 + 1,\n        });\n      }\n    };\n\n    const handleResize = (entries: ResizeObserverEntry[]) => {\n      for (const entry of entries) {\n        width = entry.contentRect.width;\n        height = entry.contentRect.height;\n        canvas.width = width;\n        canvas.height = height;\n        initDots();\n      }\n    };\n\n    const resizeObserver = new ResizeObserver(handleResize);\n    resizeObserver.observe(container);\n\n    // Initial setup\n    width = container.clientWidth;\n    height = container.clientHeight;\n    canvas.width = width;\n    canvas.height = height;\n    initDots();\n\n    // Mouse interaction relative to canvas\n    const handleMouseMove = (e: MouseEvent) => {\n      const rect = canvas.getBoundingClientRect();\n      mouse.current.x = e.clientX - rect.left;\n      mouse.current.y = e.clientY - rect.top;\n    };\n\n    const handleMouseLeave = () => {\n      mouse.current.x = null;\n      mouse.current.y = null;\n    };\n\n    canvas.addEventListener('mousemove', handleMouseMove);\n    canvas.addEventListener('mouseleave', handleMouseLeave);\n\n    const animate = () => {\n      ctx.fillStyle = backgroundColor;\n      ctx.fillRect(0, 0, width, height);\n\n      // Update dots\n      dots.current.forEach(dot => {\n        dot.x += dot.vx;\n        dot.y += dot.vy;\n\n        // Bounce off walls\n        if (dot.x < 0 || dot.x > width) dot.vx *= -1;\n        if (dot.y < 0 || dot.y > height) dot.vy *= -1;\n\n        ctx.beginPath();\n        ctx.arc(dot.x, dot.y, dot.radius, 0, Math.PI * 2);\n        ctx.fillStyle = dotColor;\n        ctx.fill();\n      });\n\n      // Connections\n      const connectDistance = 80;\n      const mouseDistance = 120;\n\n      for (let i = 0; i < dots.current.length; i++) {\n        for (let j = i + 1; j < dots.current.length; j++) {\n          const dx = dots.current[i].x-dots.current[j].x;\n          const dy = dots.current[i].y-dots.current[j].y;\n          const dist = Math.sqrt(dx * dx + dy * dy);\n\n          if (dist < connectDistance) {\n            ctx.beginPath();\n            ctx.moveTo(dots.current[i].x, dots.current[i].y);\n            ctx.lineTo(dots.current[j].x, dots.current[j].y);\n            const opacity = 1 - dist / connectDistance;\n            ctx.strokeStyle = `rgba(${lineColor}, ${opacity})`;\n            ctx.lineWidth = 0.5;\n            ctx.stroke();\n          }\n        }\n      }\n\n      // Mouse connections\n      if (mouse.current.x !== null && mouse.current.y !== null) {\n        dots.current.forEach(dot => {\n          const dx = dot.x-mouse.current.x!;\n          const dy = dot.y-mouse.current.y!;\n          const dist = Math.sqrt(dx * dx + dy * dy);\n\n          if (dist < mouseDistance) {\n            ctx.beginPath();\n            ctx.moveTo(dot.x, dot.y);\n            ctx.lineTo(mouse.current.x!, mouse.current.y!);\n            const opacity = 1 - dist / mouseDistance;\n            ctx.strokeStyle = `rgba(${lineColor}, ${opacity})`;\n            ctx.lineWidth = 0.8;\n            ctx.stroke();\n          }\n        });\n      }\n\n      animationFrameId.current = requestAnimationFrame(animate);\n    };\n\n    animate();\n\n    return () => {\n      if (animationFrameId.current) {\n        cancelAnimationFrame(animationFrameId.current);\n      }\n      canvas.removeEventListener('mousemove', handleMouseMove);\n      canvas.removeEventListener('mouseleave', handleMouseLeave);\n      resizeObserver.disconnect();\n    };\n  }, [backgroundColor, dotColor, lineColor, density]);\n\n  return (\n    <div ref={containerRef} className={`relative w-full h-full overflow-hidden ${className}`}>\n      <canvas ref={canvasRef} className="block" />\n    </div>\n  );\n};\n\nexport default PlexusShape;\n\n// --- 4. CORE UI COMPONENTS ---\n\n// 4.1 CIRCUITRY WIDGET FRAME\n// COMPONENT: Circuitry Widget Architecture\n// CONTAINER: Outer Frame (24px Chamfer, 1px Gray Border)\n// OVERLAYS:\n// - 1px Inset Background (Black)\n// - SVG Tech Accents (1px Stroke, Neon Pink)\n// - Plexus Particle Layer\n\ninterface ShowcaseCardProps {\n    children: React.ReactNode;\n    className?: string;\n    title: string;\n    icon: React.ReactNode;\n    code?: string;\n    description?: string;\n}\n\nconst CircuitryCard: React.FC<ShowcaseCardProps> = ({ children, className, title, icon, code, description }) => {\n    const chamferSize = "24px";\n\n    // CLIP PATH for Backgrounds (Matches the border logic)\n    const clipPathValue = `polygon(\n    ${ chamferSize } 0,\n    100% 0,\n    100% calc(100% - ${ chamferSize }),\n    calc(100% - ${ chamferSize }) 100%,\n    0 100%,\n    0 ${ chamferSize }\n)`;\n\n    return (\n        <div className={`relative flex flex-col ${ className } group isolate`}>\n            {/* 1. Background Layers (Clipped) */}\n            <div\n                className="absolute inset-0 bg-[var(--bg-main)] transition-colors duration-300"\n                style={{ clipPath: clipPathValue }}\n            />\n            <div\n                className="absolute inset-[1px] bg-[var(--bg-card-solid)] z-0 overflow-hidden"\n                style={{ clipPath: clipPathValue }}\n            >\n                {/* Universal Dark Pink Plexus Background */}\n                <div className="absolute inset-0 z-0 pointer-events-none">\n                    <PlexusShape\n                        backgroundColor="#000000"\n                        dotColor="#ec028b"\n                        lineColor="236, 2, 139"\n                        density={30}\n                        className="h-full w-full relative z-0"\n                    />\n                    <div className="absolute inset-0 bg-black/60 z-10" />\n                </div>\n            </div>\n\n            {/* 2. BORDER CONSTRUCTION (Manual Placement for Perfect Control) \n                Target: Pink on Left/Right. Gray on Chamfers/Top/Bottom. Pink Accent on Top-Left Corner.\n            */}\n\n            {/* Left Border (Gray) */}\n            <div className="absolute left-0 top-6 bottom-0 w-[1px] bg-gray-700 z-10" />\n\n            {/* Top-Left Chamfer (Gray Base) */}\n            <svg className="absolute top-0 left-0 w-6 h-6 z-10 overflow-visible pointer-events-none">\n                <line x1="0" y1="24" x2="24" y2="0" stroke="#374151" strokeWidth="1" strokeLinecap="square" />\n            </svg>\n\n            {/* TL Chamfer Accent (Pink Segment) */}\n            <svg className="absolute top-0 left-0 w-6 h-6 z-20 overflow-visible pointer-events-none">\n                <line x1="8" y1="16" x2="16" y2="8" stroke="#ec028b" strokeWidth="2" strokeLinecap="square" className="drop-shadow-[0_0_3px_rgba(236,2,139,0.8)]" />\n            </svg>\n\n            {/* Right Border (Gray) */}\n            <div className="absolute right-0 top-0 bottom-6 w-[1px] bg-gray-700 z-10" />\n\n            {/* Top Border (Gray) - Starts after chamfer */}\n            <div className="absolute left-6 right-0 top-0 h-[1px] bg-gray-700 z-10" />\n\n            {/* Bottom Border (Gray) - Ends before chamfer */}\n            <div className="absolute left-0 right-6 bottom-0 h-[1px] bg-gray-700 z-10" />\n\n            {/* Bottom-Right Chamfer (Gray Base) */}\n            <svg className="absolute bottom-0 right-0 w-6 h-6 z-10 overflow-visible pointer-events-none">\n                <line x1="0" y1="24" x2="24" y2="0" stroke="#374151" strokeWidth="1" strokeLinecap="square" />\n            </svg>\n\n            {/* BR Chamfer Accent (Pink Segment) */}\n            <svg className="absolute bottom-0 right-0 w-6 h-6 z-20 overflow-visible pointer-events-none">\n                <line x1="8" y1="16" x2="16" y2="8" stroke="#ec028b" strokeWidth="2" strokeLinecap="square" className="drop-shadow-[0_0_3px_rgba(236,2,139,0.8)]" />\n            </svg>\n\n\n            {/* 3. Card Content */}\n            <div className="relative z-20 p-6 flex flex-col h-full text-[var(--text-main)]">\n                <div className="flex items-center gap-3 mb-6 border-b border-[var(--border-color)] pb-4">\n                    <div className="text-rhive-pink p-2 bg-rhive-pink/10 rounded-sm border border-rhive-pink/20">\n                        {icon}\n                    </div>\n                    <h3 className="text-xl font-bold text-[var(--text-main)] tracking-tight">{title}</h3>\n                </div>\n\n                <div className="flex-grow">\n                    {children}\n                </div>\n            </div>\n        </div>\n    );\n};\n\n// 4.2 EFFICIENCY NUMBER TOGGLE (Chamfered Inputs)\nconst NumberToggle = ({ options, selected, onChange }) => (\n  <div className="flex gap-2">\n    {options.map(opt => (\n      <button \n        key={opt}\n        onClick={() => onChange(opt)}\n        className={`relative w-10 h-10 flex items-center justify-center text-sm font-bold transition-all duration-200 group\n          ${selected === opt ? 'text-white' : 'text-[var(--text-muted)] hover:text-[var(--text-main)]'}`}\n      >\n        <div\n            className={`absolute inset-0 transition-colors ${selected === opt ? 'bg-rhive-pink' : 'bg-[var(--bg-card-translucent)]'}`}\n            style={{ clipPath: "polygon(6px 0, 100% 0, 100% calc(100% - 6px), calc(100% - 6px) 100%, 0 100%, 0 6px)" }}\n        />\n        <svg className="absolute inset-0 w-full h-full pointer-events-none">\n            <path\n                d="M 6 0 L 40 0 L 40 34 L 34 40 L 0 40 L 0 6 Z"\n                fill="none"\n                stroke={selected === opt ? "#ec028b" : "var(--border-color)"}\n                strokeWidth="1"\n            />\n        </svg>\n        <span className="relative z-10">{opt}</span>\n      </button>\n    ))}\n  </div>\n);\n\n// --- 5. DESIGN PRINCIPLES ---\n// 1. Chamfers: Every major container must have 24px chamfers on Top-Left and Bottom-Right.\n// 2. Neon Accents: Use #ec028b (Rhive Pink) sparingly for interactive "active" states or micro-accents.\n// 3. Typography: Titles use Rubik (700/800), Data uses Monospace, Reports use EB Garamond.\n// 4. Motion: Use 'fade-in' animation on page load. Pulse effects on active status indicators.\n\n\n

cascading or rolling down the website and gathering on the proper materials in the picture at the bottom of the page. that would be really cool.  That concept is not just "cool"—it is actually a defined pinnacle of modern "scrollytelling" architecture designed to differentiate high-end brands like RHIVE from standard contractors.\nBased on the Digital Architectural Engineering Master Plan and current web animation standards, here is how that specific vision—granules and membrane rolls cascading into a final image—would be technically executed to function as a high-performance feature rather than just a gimmick.\n1. The "Granule Waterfall" (Residential Section)\nFor the roofing granules, you are describing a WebGL Particle System. This goes beyond simple video; it is a physics simulation tied to the user's scroll.\nHow it Works: As the user scrolls down the "Residential" section, thousands of tiny 3D points (representing granules) are generated at the top of the screen. Using a library like Three.js, these particles fall based on a simulated gravity formula ($y = 0.5 \cdot g \cdot p^2$), making them feel heavy and real 1-3.\nThe "Gathering" Effect: This is the critical "magic" moment you mentioned. As the particles reach the bottom of the section, they don't just disappear. They "lerp" (linearly interpolate) from their chaotic falling position to specific, fixed $x,y$ coordinates. Effectively, the chaotic granules mathematically assemble themselves like a puzzle to form the high-resolution pixel data of a completed "After" photo of a residential roof 2.\n2. The "Membrane Roll" (Commercial Section)\nFor the rolls of membrane (TPO/PVC) used in commercial roofing, the animation style shifts to match the material—smooth, continuous, and engineered.\nThe Mechanism: Instead of particles, this would utilize CSS View Timelines or GSAP ScrollTrigger. As the user scrolls, a 3D-rendered roll of TPO would visually "unroll" down the circuitry paths of the website interface 4, 5.\nThe Circuitry Connection: The white membrane could visually trace the "circuit lines" of your Tech-Noir aesthetic, turning the abstract digital lines into physical roofing material. This creates a visual metaphor: RHIVE's technology (circuitry) literally lays the foundation for the physical roof 6, 7.\n3. Why This Wins (The "Apple" Standard)\nThis specific type of interaction moves the website from a "brochure" to a "Digital Experience."\nMicro-Commitments: Every pixel the user scrolls creates a reaction (falling granules or unrolling membrane). This gives the user a sense of control and releases small amounts of dopamine, keeping them engaged all the way to the bottom of the page 8, 9.\nVisual Metaphor: It subtly teaches the customer the difference between the two products without words: Granules are granular and detail-oriented (Residential), while Membrane is seamless and expansive (Commercial) 7.\nBy implementing this, the website acts as a "Kinetic Document," proving RHIVE's mastery over both materials and technology before the customer even requests a quote 10, 11.\n\n

Columns: [**Task:** Analyze the building solar potential JSON data below, perform calculations, and output results *only* in the specified format block. Use calculation tools if available and necessary. Do not include *any* text before or after the formatted block.

**Input Data Check:**
* Verify the JSON contains: `wholeRoofStats.areaMeters2` and an array `roofSegmentStats`.
* Verify each element in `roofSegmentStats` contains `stats.areaMeters2` and `pitchDegrees`.
* If essential data is missing or the structure is incorrect, output *only* the text: 'Error: Missing required data in JSON.'

**Actions & Calculations (Use 1 meter = 3.28084 feet for conversions):**
1.  **SQ:** Calculate Total Squares: (`wholeRoofStats.areaMeters2` * (3.28084^2)) / 100. Round the result to 2 decimal places. (1 Square = 100 sq ft).
2.  **FACETS:** Count elements in `roofSegmentStats`.
3.  **AVG_PITCH:** If FACETS > 0, calculate the simple arithmetic average of all `pitchDegrees` in `roofSegmentStats`. Convert using Rise = round(12 * tan(radians(average_degrees)), standard rounding 0.5 up). Format as '[Rise]/12'. If calculation fails (e.g., due to invalid pitch data), use 'Error'.
4.  **DETAIL Table:** If FACETS > 0, create the table. For each facet (1-based index):
    * FACET: 1-based index number.
    * SQ's: Calculate (`stats.areaMeters2` * (3.28084^2)) / 100. Round to 2 decimals. If area is missing/invalid, use 'N/A'.
    * PITCH: Convert `pitchDegrees` using Rise = round(12 * tan(radians(pitchDegrees)), standard rounding 0.5 up). Format as '[Rise]/12'. If pitch is missing/invalid, use 'N/A'.

    ```
    SQ: [Result from Action 1]
    AVG_PITCH: N/A
    FACETS: 0
    DETAIL:
    FACET	SQ's	PITCH
    ```
