Dear RHIVE Team,
I am pleased to introduce the updated "RHIVE Project Savings Promotion" (RPSP). This is a strategic initiative designed to provide real cost savings to our clients while improving our own operational efficiency.
It is crucial to clarify that the RPSP is not a high-pressure tactic to force a signature, nor is it a scheme for quick sales. It is a transparency tool based on hard data.
The Purpose: Data-Driven Growth After extensive analysis, our internal systems have evaluated the data on our customer acquisition and project lifecycles. The conclusion is clear: To maximize our time, marketing budget, operational efficiency, and customer satisfaction, we must fundamentally change how we handle the 'decision phase' of a project.
Statistically, the RPSP is the single most effective mechanism we have to give back to our clients while simultaneously fueling our growth.
The Data: When we eliminate the high costs of long-term follow-up and marketing nurture (what we call "The Chase"), our efficiency skyrockets.
The Solution: Rather than keeping that margin, we believe in fairness: We pass those specific savings back to the client. This allows us to grow with every possible project by reinvesting our time into service rather than administration.
How It Works
The RPSP is applicable only for clients who are ready to proceed efficiently. This allows us to streamline our costs and pass the benefit directly to them.
Residential Projects: We offer an "Efficiency Credit" of 10% (up to $1,000). This credit removes the "nurture budget" from their quote.
The Referral Request: We also ask these clients to "share the secret" with their neighbors—encouraging them to get other bids first so they can see that our efficiency pricing beats the competition.
Commercial Projects: We use a Tiered Efficiency Matrix for projects approved within 72 hours.
The Logic: This timeline protects us from administrative bloat and protects the client from material inflation. This applies to their entire portfolio, allowing us to scale the savings for property managers.
Integrity and Standards
While this tool is powerful, maintaining integrity is mandatory.
No "Fake" Prices: Our standard prices are determined by the quality and value we deliver. The RPSP is strictly a credit for removed administrative costs.
Consistency: This must be offered to all clients during the initial presentation. You must explain it clearly so they understand it is a reward for efficiency, not a random discount.
No Pressure: Always remind the client of their 3-Day Right to Rescission. This is their safety net. It proves that we are not trying to trap them, but rather trying to help them lock in the best price safely.
Conclusion
The RPSP aims to provide a fair outcome for our clients while optimizing our business. By explaining this clearly, you help our customers feel like partners in our growth rather than targets of a sale.
If you have any questions on how to present this, please reach out. Let's continue to set the standard for transparency in our industry.
Best regards,
Michael Robinson
CEO, RHIVE Construction

Q&A

Q&A: Resolute Project Savings Promotion (RPSP)

Can customers email the proposal to avoid a follow-up visit?
Unfortunately, no. Experience shows that immediate review of proposal details before finalizing is crucial for customer satisfaction. This policy ensures no detail or promise is forgotten, and prevents confusion with other contractors.

Can customers physically bring the proposal to our office to qualify for savings?
Again, the answer is no. Proper communication and avoiding confusion is best achieved when project details are reviewed primarily by all decision makers

What if customers claim the RPSP creates high-pressure sales?
If this issue arises, the RPSP or the customer's rights under the Three-Day Cancellation Disclosure may not have been clearly explained. The RPSP is for customers ready to proceed without feeling rushed. Make sure to clarify this.

How to respond to customers who may reject us if they don't receive savings when they decide to buy?
This suggests a trust issue or misunderstanding of the RPSP. It's unlikely a customer would dismiss a top-notch, certified contractor over small savings. Establish trust, get to know the customer better, and clarify the RPSP.

Can we extend the Three-Day rule for customers who need more time?
Yes, if permissible by state law, the proposal can be extended. If extra time is needed for funding, include the term "This proposal is contingent upon funding. The company reserves the right to reject the proposal if funding is delayed more than 30 days."

What about customers who need time to decide on color or visit one of our job sites?
Generally, serious customers can make these decisions within the Three-Day rule. If an exception is needed, include the term "This proposal is contingent upon the Owner making a final color or style decision. The company reserves the right to reject the proposal if that decision is delayed more than 30 days."

RPSP: The Key to 100% Customer Satisfaction

To: All Team Members
From: CEO
Re: RPSP - Enhancing Customer Satisfaction

Our RPSP has proven to be the key to achieving 100% customer satisfaction. Initially tested to measure its financial benefits, the RPSP proved immediately beneficial. It reaffirmed that sales is a numbers game—the more bids, the more work. The results were impressive.

Moreover, data now shows that customer satisfaction is enhanced due to the RPSP. The common disputes between contractors and customers—communication issues, unmet expectations, and unforeseen costs—are virtually eliminated by employing the RPSP.

By incentivizing immediate decision-making, we're reducing "memory loss" that arises when contracts are signed long after the proposal is discussed. This helps eliminate misunderstandings over forgotten promises or confused details.

We strongly recommend all members utilize the RPSP to reduce sales costs, increase volume, and improve customer relations. The best time for a customer to finalize a proposal is at the presentation when all details are fresh in their minds.

Sincerely,
Michael Robinson, CEO
Resolute Construction Inc.

Suggested Contract Terms

We've outlined some contract terms for your consideration:

Acceptance/Rejection: The company has the right to refuse or cancel part or all of this agreement due to poor payment performance or low credit rating from the customer.

Approval: This proposal can be modified without notice and is automatically withdrawn on the 30th day of issuance if not approved.

Alternate Bids: Customers have the option to seek alternative bids for additional work, as long as it doesn't delay the completion of the project.

Customer Satisfaction: Invoice presentation means we consider the project complete. Upon receiving it, the customer must promptly inspect the work and either approve or disapprove of it.

Company Responsibility: We will provide the necessary labor, materials, and sales tax for the materials to finish the work as specified. The company reserves the right to substitute materials of equal quality and kind, and retains ownership of any surplus or salvageable materials.

Company Insurance: We will provide Workers Compensation, Public Liability, Property Damage, and Complete Operations insurance for the project unless a general contractor, subcontractor, or the owner provides it. Insurance will cover any damage to the building or its contents during construction or the warranty period, and our liability is limited to the coverage provided.

Alternate Bids: Customers can obtain alternative bids for additional work, provided it doesn't unduly delay project completion. The company is indemnified for any damage to the property during the bidding period. In emergencies, if the customer is away from the work site, we're authorized to proceed without formal notification, but are responsible for documenting any additional work performed.

Customer Satisfaction: Presentation of the invoice signifies the company's view that the project is complete. Upon receipt, the customer is obligated to promptly conduct a final inspection and approve or disapprove the work by returning the Customer Satisfaction Rating Form or 
informing the company in writing of any work considered incomplete or unsatisfactory. If no notice of dissatisfaction is received within a week, the project is deemed completed and accepted by the customer.

Company Responsibility: The company will provide the necessary labor, materials, and sales tax on materials required to complete the work as outlined. The company may, at its discretion, substitute materials used in the work, as long as the substituted materials are of the same kind and quality. All surplus or recoverable materials remain the property of the company.
